## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species' concentration as a function of time and current concentration. The rate law dA/dt typically follows power-law dependence on concentration (nth-order kinetics), but explicit time dependence may arise from coupled reaction systems where intermediates have been eliminated.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with constant product concentration)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturating kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (autocatalytic reaction network)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Coupled system reduced: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A * exp(c2 * t) (elimination of intermediate with exponential time profile)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (complex multi-step mechanism)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Sigmoidal cooperative: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative kinetics)
- Time-modulated decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * t) (linearly changing rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power-law dependence → dA_dt = c*A^n indicates nth-order elementary reaction step or effective overall order
- Linear dependence on A with nonzero intercept → suggests reversible reaction or constant source/sink term from other species
- Rational function of A (A/(K+A)) → indicates enzyme saturation, surface adsorption, or Langmuir-type mechanism
- Product of A with exponential in t → suggests coupled kinetics where an intermediate follows exponential decay/growth
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → indicates parallel reaction pathways or complex mechanism with competing steps
- Negative coefficient on leading A term → net consumption of species A (reactant being depleted)
- Square root dependence A**0.5 → may indicate chain reaction mechanism with radical intermediates
- Ratio of polynomials in A → Michaelis-Menten or Langmuir-Hinshelwood surface reaction mechanisms
- Explicit time dependence without A → external forcing, photolysis with varying light intensity, or zero-order driven process
- Logarithmic dependence log(A) → rare but can arise in Elovich-type kinetics for heterogeneous surface reactions
